"capitalist" Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martin_Kitchen_2006._p._205_98-2"><a href="#cite_note-Martin_Kitchen_2006._p._205-98">[98]</a></sup> He believed that the "Spirit of 1914" manifested itself in the concept of the "People\'s League of National Socialism".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bernd-R&#252;diger_H&#252;ppauf_1997._p._92_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bernd-R&#252;diger_H&#252;ppauf_1997._p._92-99">[99]</a></sup> This National Socialism was a form of <a href="/wiki/State_socialism" title="State socialism">state socialism</a> that rejected the "idea of boundless freedom" and promoted an economy that would serve the whole of Germany under the leadership of the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bernd-R&#252;diger_H&#252;ppauf_1997._p._92_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bernd-R&#252;diger_H&#252;ppauf_1997._p._92-99">[99]</a></sup> This National Socialism was opposed to capitalism due to the components that were against "the national interest" of Germany, but insisted that National Socialism would strive for greater efficiency in the economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bernd-R&#252;diger_H&#252;ppauf_1997._p._92_99-2"><a href="#cite_note-Bernd-R&#252;diger_H&#252;ppauf_1997._p._92-99">[99]</a></sup> Plenge advocated an authoritarian, rational ruling elite to develop National Socialism through a hierarchical <a href="/wiki/Technocracy" title="Technocracy">technocratic</a> state,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thomas_Rohkr&#228;mer_2007._p._130_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas_Rohkr&#228;mer_2007._p._130-100">[100]</a></sup> and his ideas were part of the basis of Nazism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martin_Kitchen_2006._p._205_98-3"><a href="#cite_note-Martin_Kitchen_2006._p._205-98">[98]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R06610,_Oswald_Spengler.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="792" data-file-width="583" decoding="async" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R06610%2C_Oswald_Spengler.jpg/170px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R06610%2C_Oswald_Spengler.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R06610%2C_Oswald_Spengler.jpg/255px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R06610%2C_Oswald_Spengler.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R06610%2C_Oswald_Spengler.jpg/340px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R06610%2C_Oswald_Spengler.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R06610,_Oswald_Spengler.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Oswald_Spengler" title="Oswald Spengler">Oswald Spengler</a>, a philosopher of history</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Oswald_Spengler" title="Oswald Spengler">Oswald Spengler</a>, a German cultural philosopher, was a major influence on Nazism, although after 1933 he became alienated from Nazism and was later condemned by the Nazis for criticising Adolf Hitler.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated16_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated16-101">[101]</a></sup> Spengler\'s conception of national socialism and a number of his political views were shared by the Nazis and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conservative_Revolutionary_movement" title="Conservative Revolutionary movement">Conservative Revolutionary movement</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated7_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated7-102">[102]</a></sup> Spengler\'s views were also popular amongst <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_fascism" title="Italian fascism">Italian Fascists</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-encyclopedia15_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-encyclopedia15-103">[103]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Spengler\'s book <i><a href="/wiki/The_Decline_of_the_West" title="The Decline of the West">The Decline of the West</a></i> (1918), written during the final months of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, addressed the supposed <a href="/wiki/Decadence" title="Decadence">decadence</a> of modern European civilization, which he claimed was caused by atomising and irreligious individualisation and <a href="/wiki/Cosmopolitanism" title="Cosmopolitanism">cosmopolitanism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated16_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated16-101">[101]</a></sup> Spengler\'s major thesis was that a law of historical development of cultures existed involving a cycle of birth, maturity, ageing and death when it reaches its final form of civilisation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated16_101-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated16-101">[101]</a></sup> Upon reaching the point of civilisation, a culture will lose its creative capacity and succumb to <a href="/wiki/Decadence" title="Decadence">decadence</a> until the emergence of "<a href="/wiki/Barbarian" title="Barbarian">barbarians</a>" creates a new epoch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated16_101-3"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated16-101">[101]</a></sup> Spengler considered the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western world</a> as having succumbed to decadence of intellect, money, <a href="/wiki/Cosmopolitanism" title="Cosmopolitanism">cosmopolitan</a> urban life, irreligious life, <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Atomization" title="wiktionary:Atomization">atomised</a> <a href="/wiki/Individualism" title="Individualism">individualisation</a> and believed that it was at the end of its biological and "spiritual" fertility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated16_101-4"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated16-101">[101]</a></sup> He believed that the "young" German nation as an imperial power would inherit the legacy of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Ancient Rome</a>, lead a restoration of value in "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bloodline" title="Bloodline">blood</a>" and instinct, while the ideals of rationalism would be revealed as absurd.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated16_101-5"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated16-101">[101]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Spengler\'s notions of "Prussian socialism" as described in his book <i><a href="/wiki/Preussentum_und_Sozialismus" title="Preussentum und Sozialismus">Preussentum und Sozialismus</a></i> ("Prussiandom and Socialism", 1919), influenced Nazism and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conservative_Revolutionary_movement" title="Conservative Revolutionary movement">Conservative Revolutionary movement</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated7_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated7-102">[102]</a></sup> Spengler wrote: "The meaning of socialism is that life is controlled not by the opposition between rich and poor, but by the rank that achievement and talent bestow. That is <i>our</i> freedom, freedom from the economic despotism of the individual".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated7_102-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated7-102">[102]</a></sup> Spengler adopted the anti-English ideas addressed by Plenge and Sombart during World War I that condemned English liberalism and English parliamentarianism while advocating a national socialism that was free from <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a> and that would connect the individual to the state through <a href="/wiki/Corporatism" title="Corporatism">corporatist</a> organisation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated16_101-6"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated16-101">[101]</a></sup> Spengler claimed that socialistic Prussian characteristics existed across Germany, including creativity, discipline, concern for the greater good, productivity and self-sacrifice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-university17_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-university17-104">[104]</a></sup> He prescribed war as a necessity by saying: "War is the eternal form of higher human existence and states exist for war: they are the expression of the will to war".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-university18_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-university18-105">[105]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1971-091-20,_Kapp-Putsch,_Marine-Brigade_Erhardt.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="539" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1971-091-20%2C_Kapp-Putsch%2C_Marine-Brigade_Erhardt.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1971-091-20%2C_Kapp-Putsch%2C_Marine-Brigade_Erhardt.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1971-091-20%2C_Kapp-Putsch%2C_Marine-Brigade_Erhardt.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1971-091-20%2C_Kapp-Putsch%2C_Marine-Brigade_Erhardt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1971-091-20%2C_Kapp-Putsch%2C_Marine-Brigade_Erhardt.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1971-091-20%2C_Kapp-Putsch%2C_Marine-Brigade_Erhardt.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1971-091-20,_Kapp-Putsch,_Marine-Brigade_Erhardt.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marinebrigade_Erhardt" title="Marinebrigade Erhardt">Marinebrigade Erhardt</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Kapp_Putsch" title="Kapp Putsch">Kapp Putsch</a> in Berlin, 1920<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> (the Marinebrigade Erhardt used the <a href="/wiki/Swastika" title="Swastika">swastika</a> as its symbol, as seen on their helmets and on the truck, which inspired the Nazi Party to adopt it as the movement\'s symbol)</div></div></div>\n<p>Spengler\'s definition of socialism did not advocate a change to property relations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated7_102-3"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated7-102">[102]</a></sup> He denounced <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a> for seeking to train the proletariat to "expropriate the expropriator", the capitalist and then to let them live a life of leisure on this expropriation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-H._Stuart_Hughes_1992._p._108_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-H._Stuart_Hughes_1992._p._108-107">[107]</a></sup> He claimed that "Marxism is the capitalism of the working class" and not true socialism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-H._Stuart_Hughes_1992._p._108_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-H._Stuart_Hughes_1992._p._108-107">[107]</a></sup> According to Spengler, true socialism would be in the form of corporatism, stating that "local corporate bodies organised according to the importance of each occupation to the people as a whole; higher representation in stages up to a supreme council of the state; mandates revocable at any time; no organised parties, no professional politicians, no periodic elections".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-transaction_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-transaction-108">[108]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Das_Dritte_Reich.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="366" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Das_Dritte_Reich.jpg/170px-Das_Dritte_Reich.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Das_Dritte_Reich.jpg/255px-Das_Dritte_Reich.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Das_Dritte_Reich.jpg/340px-Das_Dritte_Reich.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Das_Dritte_Reich.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The book <i><a href="/wiki/Das_Dritte_Reich" title="Das Dritte Reich">Das Dritte Reich</a></i> (1923), translated as "The Third Reich", by <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Moeller_van_den_Bruck" title="Arthur Moeller van den Bruck">Arthur Moeller van den Bruck</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Wilhelm Stapel, an antisemitic German intellectual, utilised Spengler\'s thesis on the cultural confrontation between Jews as whom Spengler described as a <a href="/wiki/Magi" title="Magi">Magian</a> people versus <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Europeans" title="Europeans">Europeans</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Faust" title="Faust">Faustian</a> people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MordecaiKaplan_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-MordecaiKaplan-109">[109]</a></sup> Stapel described Jews as a landless nomadic people in pursuit of an international culture whereby they can integrate into Western civilisation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MordecaiKaplan_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-MordecaiKaplan-109">[109]</a></sup> As such, Stapel claims that Jews have been attracted to "international" versions of socialism, pacifism or capitalism because as a landless people the Jews have transgressed various national cultural boundaries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MordecaiKaplan_109-2"><a href="#cite_note-MordecaiKaplan-109">[109]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Arthur_Moeller_van_den_Bruck" title="Arthur Moeller van den Bruck">Arthur Moeller van den Bruck</a> was initially the dominant figure of the Conservative Revolutionaries influenced Nazism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-university19_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-university19-110">[110]</a></sup> He rejected <a href="/wiki/Reactionary" title="Reactionary">reactionary</a> conservatism while proposing a new state that he coined the "Third Reich", which would unite all classes under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Authoritarian" title="Authoritarian">authoritarian</a> rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-macmillan_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-macmillan-111">[111]</a></sup> Van den Bruck advocated a combination of the nationalism of the right and the socialism of the left.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-millennial_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-millennial-112">[112]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">Fascism</a> was a major influence on Nazism. The seizure of power by Italian Fascist leader Benito Mussolini in the <a href="/wiki/March_on_Rome" title="March on Rome">March on Rome</a> in 1922 drew admiration by Hitler, who less than a month later had begun to model himself and the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a> upon Mussolini and the Fascists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw1999182_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw1999182-113">[113]</a></sup> Hitler presented the Nazis as a form of German fascism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fulda,_Bernhard_2009._p._65_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fulda,_Bernhard_2009._p._65-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carlsten,_F._L._1982._p._80_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carlsten,_F._L._1982._p._80-115">[115]</a></sup> In November 1923, the Nazis attempted a "March on Berlin" modelled after the March on Rome, which resulted in the failed <a href="/wiki/Beer_Hall_Putsch" title="Beer Hall Putsch">Beer Hall Putsch</a> in <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dissolution_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-dissolution-116">[116]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hitler spoke of Nazism being indebted to the success of Fascism\'s rise to power in Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hugh_R._Trevor-Roper_2008._p10_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hugh_R._Trevor-Roper_2008._p10-117">[117]</a></sup> In a private conversation in 1941, Hitler said that "the brown shirt would probably not have existed without the black shirt", the "brown shirt" referring to the Nazi militia and the "black shirt" referring to the Fascist militia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hugh_R._Trevor-Roper_2008._p10_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hugh_R._Trevor-Roper_2008._p10-117">[117]</a></sup> He also said in regards to the 1920s: "If Mussolini had been outdistanced by Marxism, I don\'t know whether we could have succeeded in holding out. At that period National Socialism was a very fragile growth".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hugh_R._Trevor-Roper_2008._p10_117-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hugh_R._Trevor-Roper_2008._p10-117">[117]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other Nazis&#8212;especially those at the time associated with the party\'s more radical wing such as <a href="/wiki/Gregor_Strasser" title="Gregor Strasser">Gregor Strasser</a>, Joseph Goebbels and Heinrich Himmler&#8212;rejected Italian Fascism, accusing it of being too conservative or capitalist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-university21_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-university21-118">[118]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Rosenberg" title="Alfred Rosenberg">Alfred Rosenberg</a> condemned Italian Fascism for being racially confused and having influences from <a href="/wiki/Philo-Semitism" title="Philo-Semitism">philosemitism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stanley_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-stanley-119">[119]</a></sup> Strasser criticised the policy of <i><a href="/wiki/F%C3%BChrerprinzip" title="F&#252;hrerprinzip">F&#252;hrerprinzip</a></i> as being created by Mussolini and considered its presence in Nazism as a foreign imported idea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stanley_G._Payne_1995._p._464_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stanley_G._Payne_1995._p._464-120">[120]</a></sup> Throughout the relationship between Nazi Germany and Fascist Italy, a number of lower-ranking Nazis scornfully viewed fascism as a conservative movement that lacked a full revolutionary potential.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stanley_G._Payne_1995._p._464_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-Stanley_G._Payne_1995._p._464-120">[120]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ideology">Ideology</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nationalism_and_racialism">Nationalism and racialism</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Nazism_and_race" title="Nazism and race">Nazism and race</a> and <a href="/wiki/Racial_policy_of_Nazi_Germany" title="Racial policy of Nazi Germany">Racial policy of Nazi Germany</a></div>\n<p>Nazism emphasized <a href="/wiki/German_nationalism" title="German nationalism">German nationalism</a>, including both <a href="/wiki/Irredentism" title="Irredentism">irredentism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Expansionism" title="Expansionism">expansionism</a>. Nazism held racial theories based upon a belief in the existence of an <a href="/wiki/Aryan_race" title="Aryan race">Aryan master race</a> that was superior to all other races. The Nazis emphasised the existence of racial conflict between the Aryan race and others&#8212;particularly Jews, whom the Nazis viewed as a mixed race that had infiltrated multiple societies and was responsible for exploitation and repression of the Aryan race. The Nazis also categorised <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a> as <i><a href="/wiki/Untermensch" title="Untermensch">Untermensch</a></i> (sub-human).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Irredentism_and_expansionism">Irredentism and expansionism</span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Lebensraum" title="Lebensraum">Lebensraum</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_R_49_Bild-0131,_Aussiedlung_von_Polen_im_Wartheland.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="549" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Bundesarchiv_R_49_Bild-0131%2C_Aussiedlung_von_Polen_im_Wartheland.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_R_49_Bild-0131%2C_Aussiedlung_von_Polen_im_Wartheland.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Bundesarchiv_R_49_Bild-0131%2C_Aussiedlung_von_Polen_im_Wartheland.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_R_49_Bild-0131%2C_Aussiedlung_von_Polen_im_Wartheland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Bundesarchiv_R_49_Bild-0131%2C_Aussiedlung_von_Polen_im_Wartheland.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_R_49_Bild-0131%2C_Aussiedlung_von_Polen_im_Wartheland.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_R_49_Bild-0131,_Aussiedlung_von_Polen_im_Wartheland.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Beginning of <i>Lebensraum</i>, the <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_Poles_by_Nazi_Germany" title="Expulsion of Poles by Nazi Germany">Nazi German expulsion of Poles</a> from <a href="/wiki/Reichsgau_Wartheland" title="Reichsgau Wartheland">central Poland</a>, 1939</div></div></div>\n<p>The German Nazi Party supported German irredentist claims to <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alsace-Lorraine" title="Alsace-Lorraine">Alsace-Lorraine</a>, the region now known as the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> and the territory known since 1919 as the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Corridor" title="Polish Corridor">Polish Corridor</a>. A major policy of the German Nazi Party was <i><a href="/wiki/Lebensraum" title="Lebensraum">Lebensraum</a></i> ("living space") for the German nation based on claims that Germany after World War I was facing an overpopulation crisis and that expansion was needed to end the country\'s overpopulation within existing confined territory, and provide resources necessary to its people\'s well-being.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stephen_J._Lee_1945._P._237_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stephen_J._Lee_1945._P._237-122">[122]</a></sup> Since the 1920s, the Nazi Party publicly promoted the expansion of Germany into territories held by the Soviet Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peter_D._Stachura_P._31_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Peter_D._Stachura_P._31-123">[123]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <i>Mein Kampf</i>, Hitler stated that <i>Lebensraum</i> would be acquired in Eastern Europe, especially Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> In his early years as the Nazi leader, Hitler had claimed that he would be willing to accept friendly relations with Russia on the tactical condition that Russia agree to return to the borders established by the German&#8211;Russian peace agreement of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk" title="Treaty of Brest-Litovsk">Treaty of Brest-Litovsk</a> signed by <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federated_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federated Socialist Republic">Russian Soviet Federated Socialist Republic</a> in 1918 which gave large territories held by Russia to German control in exchange for peace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peter_D._Stachura_P._31_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-Peter_D._Stachura_P._31-123">[123]</a></sup> In 1921, Hitler had commended the Treaty of Brest-Litovsk as opening the possibility for restoration of relations between Germany and Russia by saying:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Through the peace with Russia the sustenance of Germany as well as the provision of work were to have been secured by the acquisition of land and soil, by access to raw materials, and by friendly relations between the two lands.</p><div class="templatequotecite">&#8212;&#8201;<cite>Adolf Hitler<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peter_D._Stachura_P._31_123-2"><a href="#cite_note-Peter_D._Stachura_P._31-123">[123]</a></sup></cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Europe_topography_map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1198" data-file-width="1473" decoding="async" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Europe_topography_map.png/220px-Europe_topography_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Europe_topography_map.png/330px-Europe_topography_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Europe_topography_map.png/440px-Europe_topography_map.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Europe_topography_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Topographical map of Europe: the Nazi Party declared support for <i><a href="/wiki/Drang_nach_Osten" title="Drang nach Osten">Drang nach Osten</a></i> (expansion of Germany east to the Ural Mountains), that is shown on the upper right side of the map as a brown diagonal line</div></div></div>\n<p>From 1921 to 1922, Hitler evoked rhetoric of both the achievement of <i>Lebensraum</i> involving the acceptance of a territorially reduced Russia as well as supporting Russian nationals in overthrowing the Bolshevik government and establishing a new Russian government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peter_D._Stachura_P._31_123-3"><a href="#cite_note-Peter_D._Stachura_P._31-123">[123]</a></sup> Hitler\'s attitudes changed by the end of 1922, in which he then supported an alliance of Germany with Britain to destroy Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peter_D._Stachura_P._31_123-4"><a href="#cite_note-Peter_D._Stachura_P._31-123">[123]</a></sup> Hitler later declared how far he intended to expand Germany into Russia:\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Asia, what a disquieting reservoir of men! The safety of Europe will not be assured until we have driven Asia back behind the Urals. No organized Russian state must be allowed to exist west of that line.</p><div class="templatequotecite">&#8212;&#8201;<cite>Adolf Hitler<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Andr&#233;_Mineau_2004._P._36_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Andr&#233;_Mineau_2004._P._36-125">[125]</a></sup></cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<p>Policy for <i>Lebensraum</i> planned mass expansion of Germany\'s borders to eastwards of the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Andr&#233;_Mineau_2004._P._36_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-Andr&#233;_Mineau_2004._P._36-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Hitler planned for the "surplus" Russian population living west of the Urals to be deported to the east of the Urals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Racial_theories">Racial theories</span></h4>\n<p>In its <a href="/wiki/Race_(human_categorization)" title="Race (human categorization)">racial categorization</a>, Nazism viewed what it called the <a href="/wiki/Aryan_race" title="Aryan race">Aryan race</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Master_race" title="Master race">master race</a> of the world&#8212;a race that was superior to all other races.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79-128">[128]</a></sup> It viewed Aryans as being in racial conflict with a mixed race people, the <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, whom the Nazis identified as a dangerous enemy of the Aryans. It also viewed a number of other peoples as dangerous to the well-being of the Aryan race. In order to preserve the perceived racial purity of the Aryan race, a set of race laws was introduced in 1935 which came to be known as the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Laws" title="Nuremberg Laws">Nuremberg Laws</a>. At first these laws only prevented sexual relations and marriages between Germans and Jews, but they were later extended to the "<a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Gypsies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">Negroes</a>, and their bastard offspring", who were described by the Nazis as people of "alien blood".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RGallately_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-RGallately-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burleigh1991_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burleigh1991-130">[130]</a></sup> Such relations between Aryans (cf. <a href="/wiki/Aryan_certificate" title="Aryan certificate">Aryan certificate</a>) and non-Aryans were now punishable under the race laws as <i><a href="/wiki/Rassenschande" title="Rassenschande">Rassenschande</a></i> or "race defilement".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RGallately_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-RGallately-129">[129]</a></sup> After the war began, the race defilement law was extended to include all foreigners (non-Germans).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMajer2003180_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMajer2003180-131">[131]</a></sup> At the bottom of the racial scale of non-Aryans were <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romanis</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavic_people" title="Slavic people">Slavs</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mineau,_Andr&#233;_2004_p._180_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mineau,_Andr&#233;_2004_p._180-132">[132]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">blacks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Simone_Gigliotti_2005._Pp._14_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Simone_Gigliotti_2005._Pp._14-133">[133]</a></sup> To maintain the "purity and strength" of the Aryan race, the Nazis eventually sought to <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">exterminate</a> Jews, Romani, Slavs and the <a href="/wiki/Physical_disability" title="Physical disability">physically</a> and <a href="/wiki/Developmental_disability" title="Developmental disability">mentally disabled</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mineau,_Andr&#233;_2004_p._180_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mineau,_Andr&#233;_2004_p._180-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Simone_Gigliotti_2005._p._14_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Simone_Gigliotti_2005._p._14-134">[134]</a></sup> Other groups deemed "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Degeneration" title="Degeneration">degenerate</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Asociality" title="Asociality">asocial</a>" who were not targeted for extermination, but were subjected to <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">exclusionary treatment</a> by the Nazi state, included <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuals</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_people_in_Nazi_Germany" title="Black people in Nazi Germany">blacks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah\'s Witnesses">Jehovah\'s Witnesses</a> and political opponents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Simone_Gigliotti_2005._p._14_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-Simone_Gigliotti_2005._p._14-134">[134]</a></sup> One of Hitler\'s ambitions at the start of the war was to <a href="/wiki/Generalplan_Ost" title="Generalplan Ost">exterminate, expel or enslave</a> most or all <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a> from <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> in order to acquire <a href="/wiki/Lebensraum" title="Lebensraum">living space</a> for German settlers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-google-135">[135]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-16748,_Ausstellung_%22Wunder_des_Lebens%22.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="552" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-16748%2C_Ausstellung_%22Wunder_des_Lebens%22.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-16748%2C_Ausstellung_%22Wunder_des_Lebens%22.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-16748%2C_Ausstellung_%22Wunder_des_Lebens%22.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-16748%2C_Ausstellung_%22Wunder_des_Lebens%22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-16748%2C_Ausstellung_%22Wunder_des_Lebens%22.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-16748%2C_Ausstellung_%22Wunder_des_Lebens%22.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-16748,_Ausstellung_%22Wunder_des_Lebens%22.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A "poster information" from the exhibition "<i>Miracle of Life</i>" in Berlin in 1935</div></div></div>\n<p>A Nazi era school textbook for German students entitled <i>Heredity and Racial Biology for Students</i> written by Jakob Graf described to students the Nazi conception of the Aryan race in a section titled "The Aryan: The Creative Force in Human History".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79-128">[128]</a></sup> Graf claimed that the original Aryans developed from Nordic peoples who invaded ancient India and launched the initial development of Aryan culture there that later spread to ancient Persia and he claimed that the Aryan presence in Persia was what was responsible for its development into an empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79_128-2"><a href="#cite_note-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79-128">[128]</a></sup> He claimed that <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">ancient Greek culture</a> was developed by Nordic peoples due to paintings of the time which showed Greeks who were tall, light-skinned, light-eyed, blond-haired people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79_128-3"><a href="#cite_note-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79-128">[128]</a></sup> He said that the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> was developed by the <a href="/wiki/Italic_peoples" title="Italic peoples">Italics</a> who were related to the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> who were also a Nordic people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79_128-4"><a href="#cite_note-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79-128">[128]</a></sup> He believed that the vanishing of the Nordic component of the populations in Greece and Rome led to their downfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79_128-5"><a href="#cite_note-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79-128">[128]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> was claimed to have developed in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a> because of the Germanic invasions that brought new Nordic blood to the Empire\'s lands, such as the presence of Nordic blood in the <a href="/wiki/Lombards" title="Lombards">Lombards</a> (referred to as Longobards in the book); that remnants of the western Goths were responsible for the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>; and that the heritage of the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a> and Germanic peoples in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> was what was responsible for its rise as a major power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79_128-6"><a href="#cite_note-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79-128">[128]</a></sup> He claimed that the rise of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> was due to its leadership by people of <a href="/wiki/Normans" title="Normans">Norman</a> descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79_128-7"><a href="#cite_note-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79-128">[128]</a></sup> He described the rise of Anglo-Saxon societies in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> as being the result of the Nordic heritage of <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Anglo-Saxons</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79_128-8"><a href="#cite_note-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79-128">[128]</a></sup> He concluded these points by saying: "Everywhere Nordic creative power has built mighty empires with high-minded ideas, and to this very day <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Aryan languages</a> and cultural values are spread over a large part of the world, though the creative Nordic blood has long since vanished in many places".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79_128-9"><a href="#cite_note-George_Lachmann_Mosse_p79-128">[128]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Buchenwald_Corpses_60623.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="944" data-file-width="1400" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Buchenwald_Corpses_60623.jpg/220px-Buchenwald_Corpses_60623.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Buchenwald_Corpses_60623.jpg/330px-Buchenwald_Corpses_60623.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Buchenwald_Corpses_60623.jpg/440px-Buchenwald_Corpses_60623.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Buchenwald_Corpses_60623.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A wagon piled high with corpses outside the crematorium in <a href="/wiki/Buchenwald_concentration_camp" title="Buchenwald concentration camp">Buchenwald concentration camp</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In Nazi Germany, the idea of creating a master race resulted in efforts to "purify" the <i>Deutsche Volk</i> through <a href="/wiki/Nazi_eugenics" title="Nazi eugenics">eugenics</a> and its culmination was the <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_sterilization" title="Compulsory sterilization">compulsory sterilization</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Involuntary_euthanasia" title="Involuntary euthanasia">involuntary euthanasia</a> of physically or mentally disabled people. After World War II, the euthanasia programme was named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Action_T4" title="Action T4">Action T4</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> The ideological justification for <a href="/wiki/Euthanasia" title="Euthanasia">euthanasia</a> was Hitler\'s view of <a href="/wiki/Sparta" title="Sparta">Sparta</a> (11th century &#8211; 195 BC) as the original <i>V&#246;lkisch</i> state and he praised Sparta\'s dispassionate destruction of congenitally deformed infants in order to maintain racial purity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pathological_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-pathological-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Social_Darwinism_in_European_and_American_Thought,_1860&#8211;1945:_nature_as_model_and_nature_as_threat_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Social_Darwinism_in_European_and_American_Thought,_1860&#8211;1945:_nature_as_model_and_nature_as_threat-138">[138]</a></sup> Some non-Aryans enlisted in Nazi organisations like the <a href="/wiki/Hitler_Youth" title="Hitler Youth">Hitler Youth</a> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a></i>, including Germans of African descent<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-experiences_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-experiences-139">[139]</a></sup> and Jewish descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> The Nazis began to implement "racial hygiene" policies as soon as they came to power. The July 1933 "Law for the Prevention of Hereditarily Diseased Offspring" prescribed compulsory sterilization for people with a range of conditions which were thought to be hereditary, such as <a href="/wiki/Schizophrenia" title="Schizophrenia">schizophrenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Epilepsy" title="Epilepsy">epilepsy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huntington%27s_chorea" title="Huntington\'s chorea">Huntington\'s chorea</a> and "<a href="/wiki/Intellectual_disability" title="Intellectual disability">imbecility</a>". Sterilization was also mandated for chronic <a href="/wiki/Alcoholism" title="Alcoholism">alcoholism</a> and other forms of <a href="/wiki/Deviance_(sociology)" title="Deviance (sociology)">social deviance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evans10_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Evans10-141">[141]</a></sup> An estimated 360,000 people were sterilised under this law between 1933 and 1939. Although some Nazis suggested that the programme should be extended to people with physical disabilities, such ideas had to be expressed carefully, given the fact that some Nazis had physical disabilities, one example being one of the most powerful figures of the regime, Joseph Goebbels, who had a deformed right leg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nazi racial theorist <a href="/wiki/Hans_F._K._G%C3%BCnther" title="Hans F. K. G&#252;nther">Hans F. K. G&#252;nther</a> argued that European peoples were divided into five races: <a href="/wiki/Nordic_race" title="Nordic race">Nordic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_race" title="Mediterranean race">Mediterranean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dinaric_race" title="Dinaric race">Dinaric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpine_race" title="Alpine race">Alpine</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Baltic_race" title="East Baltic race">East Baltic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baum2006_156_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Baum2006_156-3">[3]</a></sup> G&#252;nther applied a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nordicism" title="Nordicism">Nordicist</a> conception in order to justify his belief that Nordics were the highest in the racial hierarchy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baum2006_156_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-Baum2006_156-3">[3]</a></sup> In his book <i><a href="/wiki/Rassenkunde_des_deutschen_Volkes" title="Rassenkunde des deutschen Volkes">Rassenkunde des deutschen Volkes</a></i> (1922) ("Racial Science of the German People"), G&#252;nther recognised Germans as being composed of all five races, but emphasized the strong Nordic heritage among them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maxwell150_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-Maxwell150-143">[143]</a></sup> Hitler read <i>Rassenkunde des deutschen Volkes</i>, which influenced his racial policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> Gunther believed that Slavs belonged to an "Eastern race" and he warned against Germans mixing with them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> The Nazis described Jews as being a racially mixed group of primarily <a href="/wiki/Armenoid_race" title="Armenoid race">Near Eastern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabid_race" title="Arabid race">Oriental</a> racial types.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weinreich111_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weinreich111-146">[146]</a></sup> Because such racial groups were concentrated outside Europe, the Nazis claimed that Jews were "racially alien" to all European peoples and that they did not have deep racial roots in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weinreich111_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-Weinreich111-146">[146]</a></sup>\n</p><p>G&#252;nther emphasized Jews\' Near Eastern racial heritage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alan_E_Steinweis_2008._P._28_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alan_E_Steinweis_2008._P._28-147">[147]</a></sup> G&#252;nther identified the mass conversion of the <a href="/wiki/Khazars" title="Khazars">Khazars</a> to <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a> in the 8th century as creating the two major branches of the Jewish people, those of primarily Near Eastern racial heritage became the <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">Ashkenazi Jews</a> (that he called Eastern Jews) while those of primarily Oriental racial heritage became the <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Sephardi Jews</a> (that he called Southern Jews).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alan_E_Steinweis_2008._P._31-32_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alan_E_Steinweis_2008._P._31-32-148">[148]</a></sup> G&#252;nther claimed that the Near Eastern type was composed of commercially spirited and artful traders, that the type held strong <a href="/wiki/Psychological_manipulation" title="Psychological manipulation">psychological manipulation</a> skills which aided them in trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alan_E_Steinweis_2008._P._28_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-Alan_E_Steinweis_2008._P._28-147">[147]</a></sup> He claimed that the Near Eastern race had been "bred not so much for the conquest and exploitation of nature as it had been for the conquest and exploitation of people".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alan_E_Steinweis_2008._P._28_147-2"><a href="#cite_note-Alan_E_Steinweis_2008._P._28-147">[147]</a></sup> G&#252;nther believed that European peoples had a racially motivated aversion to peoples of Near Eastern racial origin and their traits, and as evidence of this he showed multiple examples of depictions of satanic figures with Near Eastern physiognomies in European art.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alan_E_Steinweis_2008._P._29_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alan_E_Steinweis_2008._P._29-149">[149]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hitler\'s conception of the Aryan <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herrenvolk" title="Herrenvolk">Herrenvolk</a></i> ("Aryan master race") excluded the vast majority of <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a> from central and eastern Europe (i.e. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nazi_crimes_against_ethnic_Poles" title="Nazi crimes against ethnic Poles">Poles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>, etc.). They were regarded as a race of men not inclined to a higher form of <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilization</a>, which was under an instinctive force that reverted them back to nature. The Nazis also regarded the Slavs as having dangerous Jewish and Asiatic, meaning <a href="/wiki/Mongols" title="Mongols">Mongol</a>, influences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> Because of this, the Nazis declared Slavs to be <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Untermenschen" title="Untermenschen">Untermenschen</a></i> ("subhumans").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> Nazi anthropologists attempted to scientifically prove the historical admixture of the Slavs who lived further East and leading Nazi racial theorist <a href="/wiki/Hans_F._K._G%C3%BCnther" title="Hans F. K. G&#252;nther">Hans G&#252;nther</a> regarded the Slavs as being primarily Nordic centuries ago but he believed that they had mixed with non-Nordic types over time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wendt2010_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wendt2010-152">[152]</a></sup> Exceptions were made for a small percentage of Slavs who the Nazis saw as descended from German settlers and therefore fit to be Germanised and considered part of the Aryan master race.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> Hitler described Slavs as "a mass of born slaves who feel the need for a master".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> The Nazi notion of Slavs as inferior served as a legitimization of their desire to create <i>Lebensraum</i> for Germans and other Germanic people in eastern Europe, where millions of Germans and other Germanic settlers would be moved into once those territories were conquered, while the original Slavic inhabitants were to be annihilated, removed or enslaved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bendersky_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bendersky-155">[155]</a></sup> Nazi Germany\'s policy changed towards Slavs in response to military manpower shortages, forced it to allow Slavs to serve in its armed forces within the occupied territories in spite of the fact that they were considered "subhuman".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hitler declared that racial conflict against Jews was necessary in order to save Germany from suffering under them and he dismissed concerns that the conflict with them was inhumane and unjust:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>We may be inhumane, but if we rescue Germany we have achieved the greatest deed in the world. We may work injustice, but if we rescue Germany then we have removed the greatest injustice in the world. We may be immoral, but if our people is rescued we have opened the way for morality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-koenigsberg_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-koenigsberg-157">[157]</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>Nazi propagandist Joseph Goebbels frequently employed antisemitic rhetoric to underline this view: "The Jew is the enemy and the destroyer of the purity of blood, the conscious destroyer of our race."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thosedamnednazis_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-thosedamnednazis-158">[158]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_class">Social class</span></h3>\n<p>National Socialist politics was based on competition and struggle as its organizing principle, and the Nazis believed that "human life consisted of eternal struggle and competition and derived its meaning from struggle and competition."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason19936_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason19936-159">[159]</a></sup> The Nazis saw this eternal struggle in military terms, and advocated a society organized like an army in order to achieve success. They promoted the idea of a national-racial "people\'s community" (<i>Volksgemeinschaft</i>) in order to accomplish "the efficient prosecution of the struggle against other peoples and states."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason19937_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason19937-160">[160]</a></sup> Like an army, the <i>Volksgemeinschaft</i> was meant to consist of a hierarchy of ranks or classes of people, some commanding and others obeying, all working together for a common goal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason19937_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason19937-160">[160]</a></sup> This concept was rooted in the writings of 19th century <i>v&#246;lkisch</i> authors who glorified medieval German society, viewing it as a "community rooted in the land and bound together by custom and tradition," in which there was neither class conflict nor selfish individualism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBendersky198540_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBendersky198540-161">[161]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nazism rejected the <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxist</a> concept of <a href="/wiki/Class_conflict" title="Class conflict">class conflict</a>, and it praised both German capitalists and German workers as essential to the <i>Volksgemeinschaft</i>. In the <i>Volksgemeinschaft</i>, social classes would continue to exist, but there would be no class conflict between them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBendersky198548_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBendersky198548-162">[162]</a></sup> Hitler said that "the capitalists have worked their way to the top through their capacity, and as the basis of this selection, which again only proves their higher race, they have a right to lead."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nicholls_245_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nicholls_245-163">[163]</a></sup> German business leaders co-operated with the Nazis during their rise to power and received substantial benefits from the Nazi state after it was established, including high profits and state-sanctioned monopolies and cartels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> Large celebrations and symbolism were used extensively to encourage those engaged in physical labour on behalf of Germany, with leading National Socialists often praising the "honour of labour", which fostered a sense of community (<i>Gemeinschaft</i>) for the German people and promoted solidarity towards the Nazi cause.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> To win workers away from Marxism, Nazi propaganda sometimes presented its expansionist foreign policy goals as a "class struggle between nations."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nicholls_245_163-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nicholls_245-163">[163]</a></sup> Bonfires were made of school children\'s differently coloured caps as symbolic of the unity of different social classes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grunberger46_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-Grunberger46-166">[166]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1922, Hitler discredited other nationalist and <a href="/wiki/Racialism" title="Racialism">racialist</a> political parties as disconnected from the mass populace, especially lower and working-class young people:\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The racialists were not capable of drawing the practical conclusions from correct theoretical judgements, especially in the Jewish Question. In this way, the German racialist movement developed a similar pattern to that of the 1880s and 1890s. As in those days, its leadership gradually fell into the hands of highly honourable, but fantastically na&#239;ve men of learning, professors, district counsellors, schoolmasters, and lawyers&#8212;in short a bourgeois, idealistic, and refined class. It lacked the warm breath of the nation\'s youthful vigour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-burleigh_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-burleigh-167">[167]</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>Nevertheless, the Nazi Party\'s voter base consisted mainly of farmers and the middle class, including groups such as Weimar government officials, school teachers, doctors, clerks, self-employed businessmen, salesmen, retired officers, engineers, and students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason199348-50_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason199348-50-168">[168]</a></sup> Their demands included lower taxes, higher prices for food, restrictions on department stores and consumer co-operatives, and reductions in social services and wages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason199349_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason199349-169">[169]</a></sup> The need to maintain the support of these groups made it difficult for the Nazis to appeal to the working class, since the working class often had opposite demands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason199349_169-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason199349-169">[169]</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 1928 onward, the Nazi Party\'s growth into a large national political movement was dependent on middle class support, and on the public perception that it "promised to side with the middle classes and to confront the economic and political power of the working class." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason199344_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason199344-170">[170]</a></sup> The financial collapse of the <a href="/wiki/White-collar_worker" title="White-collar worker">white collar</a> middle-class of the 1920s figures much in their strong support of Nazism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burleigh,_2000._p._77_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burleigh,_2000._p._77-171">[171]</a></sup> Although the Nazis continued to make appeals to "the German worker," historian Timothy Mason concludes that "Hitler had nothing but slogans to offer the working class."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason199348_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason199348-172">[172]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sex_and_gender">Sex and gender</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Nazi_Germany" title="Women in Nazi Germany">Women in Nazi Germany</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pflichten_der_polen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="945" data-file-width="1452" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Pflichten_der_polen.jpg/220px-Pflichten_der_polen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Pflichten_der_polen.jpg/330px-Pflichten_der_polen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Pflichten_der_polen.jpg/440px-Pflichten_der_polen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pflichten_der_polen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Obligations of Polish workers in Germany, warning them of the death penalty for any sexual relations between Germans and Poles</div></div></div>\n<p>Nazi ideology advocated excluding women from political involvement and confining them to the spheres of "<a href="/wiki/Kinder,_K%C3%BCche,_Kirche" title="Kinder, K&#252;che, Kirche">Kinder, K&#252;che, Kirche</a>" (Children, Kitchen, Church).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> Many women enthusiastically supported the regime, but formed their own internal hierarchies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> Hitler\'s own opinion on the matter of women in Nazi Germany was that while other eras of German history had experienced the development and liberation of the female mind, the National Socialist goal was essentially singular in that it wished for them to produce a child.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> Based on this theme, Hitler once remarked about women that "with every child that she brings into the world, she fights her battle for the nation. The man stands up for the <i>Volk</i>, exactly as the woman stands up for the family".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> Proto-natalist programs in Nazi Germany offered favourable loans and grants to newlyweds and encouraged them to give birth to offspring by providing them with additional incentives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Birth_control" title="Birth control">Contraception</a> was discouraged for racially valuable women in Nazi Germany and <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">abortion</a> was forbidden by strict legal mandates, including prison sentences for women who sought them as well as prison sentences for doctors who performed them, whereas abortion for racially "undesirable" persons was encouraged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup>\n</p><p>While unmarried until the very end of the regime, Hitler often made excuses about his busy life hindering any chance for marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> Among National Socialist ideologues, marriage was valued not for moral considerations but because it provided an optimal breeding environment. <i><a href="/wiki/Reichsf%C3%BChrer-SS" title="Reichsf&#252;hrer-SS">Reichsf&#252;hrer-SS</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Himmler" title="Heinrich Himmler">Heinrich Himmler</a> reportedly told a confidant that when he established the <i><a href="/wiki/Lebensborn" title="Lebensborn">Lebensborn</a></i> program, an organisation that would dramatically increase the birth rate of "Aryan" children through extramarital relations between women classified as racially pure and their male equals, he had only the purest male "conception assistants" in mind.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since the Nazis extended the <i><a href="/wiki/Rassenschande" title="Rassenschande">Rassenschande</a></i> ("race defilement") law to all foreigners at the beginning of the war,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMajer2003180_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMajer2003180-131">[131]</a></sup> pamphlets were issued to German women which ordered them to avoid sexual relations with foreign workers who were brought to Germany and the pamphlets also ordered German women to view these same foreign workers as a danger to their blood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rupp1978_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rupp1978-182">[182]</a></sup> Although the law was applicable to both genders, German women were punished more severely for having sexual relations with foreign <a href="/wiki/Forced_labour_under_German_rule_during_World_War_II" title="Forced labour under German rule during World War II">forced labourers</a> in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> The Nazis issued the <a href="/wiki/Polish_decrees" title="Polish decrees">Polish decrees</a> on 8 March 1940 which contained regulations concerning the Polish forced labourers (<a href="/wiki/Zivilarbeiter" title="Zivilarbeiter">Zivilarbeiter</a>) who were brought to Germany during World War II. One of the regulations stated that any Pole "who has sexual relations with a German man or woman, or approaches them in any other improper manner, will be punished by death".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gellately2001_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gellately2001-184">[184]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the decrees were enacted, Himmler stated:\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Fellow Germans who engage in sexual relations with male or female civil workers of the <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Polish</a> nationality, commit other immoral acts or engage in love affairs shall be arrested immediately.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>The Nazis later issued similar regulations against the Eastern Workers <i>(<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ost-Arbeiter" title="Ost-Arbeiter">Ost-Arbeiters</a>)</i>, including the imposition of the death penalty if they engaged in sexual relations with German persons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gellately1990_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gellately1990-186">[186]</a></sup> Heydrich issued a decree on 20 February 1942 which declared that sexual intercourse between a German woman and a Russian worker or prisoner of war would result in the Russian man being punished with the death penalty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evans2012_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-Evans2012-187">[187]</a></sup> Another decree issued by Himmler on 7 December 1942 stated that any "unauthorised sexual intercourse" would result in the death penalty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMajer2003369_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMajer2003369-188">[188]</a></sup> Because the Law for the Protection of German Blood and German Honour did not permit capital punishment for race defilement, special courts were convened in order to allow the death penalty to be imposed in some cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMajer2003331&#8211;332_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMajer2003331&#8211;332-189">[189]</a></sup> German women accused of race defilement were marched through the streets with their head shaven and placards detailing their crimes were placed around their necks<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stephenson2001_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stephenson2001-190">[190]</a></sup> and those convicted of race defilement were sent to concentration camps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rupp1978_182-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rupp1978-182">[182]</a></sup> When Himmler reportedly asked Hitler what the punishment should be for German girls and German women who were found guilty of race defilement with prisoners of war (POWs), he ordered that "every POW who has relations with a German girl or a German would be shot" and the German woman should be publicly humiliated by "having her hair shorn and being sent to a concentration camp".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Longerich2012_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-Longerich2012-191">[191]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/League_of_German_Girls" title="League of German Girls">League of German Girls</a> was particularly regarded as instructing girls to avoid race defilement, which was treated with particular importance for young females.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Opposition_to_homosexuality">Opposition to homosexuality</span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persecution_of_homosexuals_in_Nazi_Germany_and_the_Holocaust" title="Persecution of homosexuals in Nazi Germany and the Holocaust">Persecution of homosexuals in Nazi Germany and the Holocaust</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Berlin_Pink_Triangle.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="1944" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Berlin_Pink_Triangle.JPG/220px-Berlin_Pink_Triangle.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Berlin_Pink_Triangle.JPG/330px-Berlin_Pink_Triangle.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Berlin_Pink_Triangle.JPG/440px-Berlin_Pink_Triangle.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Berlin_Pink_Triangle.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Homophobia: Berlin memorial to homosexual victims of the Holocaust: <i>Totgeschlagen&#8212;Totgeschwiegen</i> (Struck Dead&#8212;Hushed Up)</div></div></div>\n<p>After the Night of the Long Knives, Hitler promoted Himmler and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS" title="SS">SS</a>, who then zealously suppressed <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a> by saying: "We must exterminate these people root and branch ... the homosexual must be eliminated".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-plant_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-plant-193">[193]</a></sup> In 1936, Himmler established the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reichszentrale_zur_Bek%C3%A4mpfung_der_Homosexualit%C3%A4t_und_Abtreibung" title="Reichszentrale zur Bek&#228;mpfung der Homosexualit&#228;t und Abtreibung">Reichszentrale zur Bek&#228;mpfung der Homosexualit&#228;t und Abtreibung</a>" ("Reich Central Office for the Combating of Homosexuality and Abortion").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Homosexualit&#228;t_und_Staatsr&#228;son._M&#228;nnlichkeit,_Homophobie_und_Politik_in_Deutschland_1900-1945_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-Homosexualit&#228;t_und_Staatsr&#228;son._M&#228;nnlichkeit,_Homophobie_und_Politik_in_Deutschland_1900-1945-194">[194]</a></sup> The Nazi regime incarcerated some 100,000 homosexuals during the 1930s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holocaust:_Gay_activists_press_for_German_apology_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-Holocaust:_Gay_activists_press_for_German_apology-195">[195]</a></sup> As concentration camp prisoners, homosexual men were forced to wear <a href="/wiki/Pink_triangle" title="Pink triangle">pink triangle</a> badges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-international_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-international-196">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-homosexuals_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-homosexuals-197">[197]</a></sup> Nazi ideology still viewed German men who were gay as a part of the Aryan <a href="/wiki/Master_race" title="Master race">master race</a>, but the Nazi regime attempted to force them into sexual and social conformity. Homosexuals were viewed as failing in their duty to procreate and reproduce for the Aryan nation. Gay men who would not change or feign a change in their <a href="/wiki/Sexual_orientation" title="Sexual orientation">sexual orientation</a> were sent to concentration camps under the "Extermination Through Work" campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Religious_aspects_of_Nazism" title="Religious aspects of Nazism">Religious aspects of Nazism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Nazi_Germany" title="Religion in Nazi Germany">Religion in Nazi Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Positive_Christianity" title="Positive Christianity">Positive Christianity</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_Christians" title="German Christians">German Christians</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_Faith_Movement" title="German Faith Movement">German Faith Movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_and_Nazi_Germany" title="Catholic Church and Nazi Germany">Catholic Church and Nazi Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kreuz_und_Adler" title="Kreuz und Adler">Kreuz und Adler</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Religious_views_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Religious views of Adolf Hitler">Religious views of Adolf Hitler</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-15234,_Berlin,_Luthertag.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="542" data-file-width="799" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-15234%2C_Berlin%2C_Luthertag.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-15234%2C_Berlin%2C_Luthertag.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-15234%2C_Berlin%2C_Luthertag.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-15234%2C_Berlin%2C_Luthertag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-15234%2C_Berlin%2C_Luthertag.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-15234%2C_Berlin%2C_Luthertag.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-15234,_Berlin,_Luthertag.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Members of the <a href="/wiki/German_Christians" title="German Christians">German Christians</a> organization celebrating Luther Day in Berlin in 1933, speech by Bishop Hossenfelder</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Orsen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="304" data-file-width="480" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Orsen.jpg/220px-Orsen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Orsen.jpg/330px-Orsen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Orsen.jpg/440px-Orsen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Orsen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hitler in 1935 with <a href="/wiki/Cesare_Orsenigo" title="Cesare Orsenigo">Cesare Orsenigo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuncio_to_Germany" title="Nuncio to Germany">nuncio to Germany</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_Program" title="National Socialist Program">Nazi Party Programme</a> of 1920 guaranteed freedom for all religious denominations which were not hostile to the State and it also endorsed <a href="/wiki/Positive_Christianity" title="Positive Christianity">Positive Christianity</a> in order to combat "the Jewish-materialist spirit".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-documents_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-documents-199">[199]</a></sup> Positive Christianity was a modified version of <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> which emphasized <a href="/wiki/Racial_hygiene" title="Racial hygiene">racial purity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNab2009182_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNab2009182-200">[200]</a></sup> The Nazis were aided by theologians such as <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Bergmann_(philosopher)" title="Ernst Bergmann (philosopher)">Ernst Bergmann</a>. In his work <i>Die 25 Thesen der Deutschreligion</i> (<i>Twenty-five Points of the German Religion</i>), Bergmann held the view that the <a href="/wiki/Old_Testament" title="Old Testament">Old Testament</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Bible</a> was inaccurate along with portions of the <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">New Testament</a>, claimed that <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a> was not a Jew but was instead of Aryan origin and he also claimed that <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> was the new <a href="/wiki/Messiah" title="Messiah">messiah</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNab2009182_200-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNab2009182-200">[200]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hitler denounced the Old Testament as "<a href="/wiki/Satan" title="Satan">Satan</a>\'s Bible" and utilising components of the New Testament he attempted to prove that Jesus was both an Aryan and an antisemite by citing passages such as <a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=John+8:44" rel="nofollow">John 8:44</a> where he noted that Jesus is yelling at "the Jews", as well as saying to them "your father is the devil" and the <a href="/wiki/Cleansing_of_the_Temple" title="Cleansing of the Temple">Cleansing of the Temple</a>, which describes Jesus\' whipping of the "Children of the Devil".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Redles60_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-Redles60-201">[201]</a></sup> Hitler claimed that the New Testament included distortions by <a href="/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle" title="Paul the Apostle">Paul the Apostle</a>, who Hitler described as a "mass-murderer turned saint".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Redles60_201-1"><a href="#cite_note-Redles60-201">[201]</a></sup> In their propaganda, the Nazis utilised the writings of <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a>, the founder of <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a>. They publicly displayed an original edition of Luther\'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/On_the_Jews_and_their_Lies" title="On the Jews and their Lies">On the Jews and their Lies</a></i> during the annual Nuremberg rallies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-understandably_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-understandably-202">[202]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baylor_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-baylor-203">[203]</a></sup> The Nazis endorsed the pro-Nazi Protestant <a href="/wiki/German_Christians" title="German Christians">German Christians</a> organization.\n</p><p>The Nazis were initially very hostile to Catholics because most Catholics supported the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Centre_Party" title="German Centre Party">German Centre Party</a>. Catholics opposed the Nazis\' promotion of <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_sterilization" title="Compulsory sterilization">compulsory sterilization</a> of those whom they deemed inferior and the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> forbade its members to vote for the Nazis. In 1933, extensive Nazi violence occurred against Catholics due to their association with the Centre Party and their opposition to the Nazi regime\'s sterilization laws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-international27_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-international27-204">[204]</a></sup> The Nazis demanded that Catholics declare their loyalty to the German state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robert_Anthony_Krieg_2004._p._4_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_Anthony_Krieg_2004._p._4-205">[205]</a></sup> In their propaganda, the Nazis used elements of Germany\'s Catholic history, in particular the German Catholic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teutonic_Knights" title="Teutonic Knights">Teutonic Knights</a> and their campaigns in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>. The Nazis identified them as "sentinels" in the East against "Slavic chaos", though beyond that symbolism, the influence of the Teutonic Knights on Nazism was limited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interaction_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-interaction-206">[206]</a></sup> Hitler also admitted that the Nazis\' night rallies were inspired by the Catholic rituals which he had witnessed during his Catholic upbringing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roger_Griffin_2005._p._85_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-Roger_Griffin_2005._p._85-207">[207]</a></sup> The Nazis did seek official reconciliation with the Catholic Church and they endorsed the creation of the pro-Nazi Catholic <i><a href="/wiki/Kreuz_und_Adler" title="Kreuz und Adler">Kreuz und Adler</a></i>, an organization which advocated a form of <a href="/wiki/National_Catholicism" title="National Catholicism">national Catholicism</a> that would reconcile the Catholic Church\'s beliefs with Nazism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robert_Anthony_Krieg_2004._p._4_205-1"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_Anthony_Krieg_2004._p._4-205">[205]</a></sup> On 20 July 1933, a concordat (<i><a href="/wiki/Reichskonkordat" title="Reichskonkordat">Reichskonkordat</a></i>) was signed between Nazi Germany and the Catholic Church, which in exchange for acceptance of the Catholic Church in Germany required German Catholics to be loyal to the German state. The Catholic Church then ended its ban on members supporting the Nazi Party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robert_Anthony_Krieg_2004._p._4_205-2"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_Anthony_Krieg_2004._p._4-205">[205]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Historian <a href="/wiki/Michael_Burleigh" title="Michael Burleigh">Michael Burleigh</a> claims that Nazism used Christianity for political purposes, but such use required that "fundamental tenets were stripped out, but the remaining diffuse religious emotionality had its uses".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roger_Griffin_2005._p._85_207-1"><a href="#cite_note-Roger_Griffin_2005._p._85-207">[207]</a></sup> Burleigh claims that Nazism\'s conception of spirituality was "self-consciously pagan and primitive".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roger_Griffin_2005._p._85_207-2"><a href="#cite_note-Roger_Griffin_2005._p._85-207">[207]</a></sup> However, historian <a href="/wiki/Roger_Griffin" title="Roger Griffin">Roger Griffin</a> rejects the claim that Nazism was primarily pagan, noting that although there were some influential neo-paganists in the Nazi Party, such as <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Himmler" title="Heinrich Himmler">Heinrich Himmler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Rosenberg" title="Alfred Rosenberg">Alfred Rosenberg</a>, they represented a minority and their views did not influence Nazi ideology beyond its use for symbolism.
